## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics): nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity) evolving in time t, which matches second-order ordinary differential equations for (nonlinear) harmonic oscillators. Typical models express dv_dt as a restoring-force term in x plus optional damping/drive terms involving v and t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (undamped free oscillator; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear damping (viscous): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped oscillator with force proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Constant/offset bias acceleration: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 (gravity/actuation bias or model mismatch offset)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with damping and drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear forced oscillator)
- Pendulum equation (exact restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle pendulum with damping; small-angle reduces to linear in x)
- Quadratic/nonlinear drag: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping at higher speeds)
- Nonlinear (amplitude-dependent) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (damping increases with displacement amplitude)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle via negative-to-positive damping transition)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness leading to parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear restoring with higher-order terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (polynomial potential expansion for strong nonlinear springs)
- State-dependent frequency (nonlinear stiffness + drive): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (alternate forcing phase choice)
- Energy-based conservative oscillator (via potential derivative): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (interpretable as dv_dt = -dV/dx with V a polynomial in x)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt depends primarily on x (odd function in x for symmetric potentials), with little/no explicit t dependence.
- Viscous dissipation → include a term linear in v; negative coefficient (absorbed into c) yields exponential decay of oscillation amplitude.
- Aerodynamic/high-Re drag → include v*Abs(v) (or other even-in-v factors times v) to model stronger damping at larger speeds.
- Hardening/softening stiffness → include x**3 (and possibly x**5) terms; sign controls whether frequency increases or decreases with amplitude.
- Large-angle pendulum behavior → use sin(c*x) rather than x; linearization emerges automatically for small x.
- Self-excited limit cycles → use state-dependent damping like (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v (negative damping near origin, positive at large |x|).
- External periodic forcing → add sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms independent of state; yields resonance peaks when drive frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance → multiply x by a periodic function of t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, representing time-varying stiffness.
- Amplitude-dependent damping → terms like x**2*v (or higher powers) indicate dissipation coupled to displacement amplitude (e.g., material hysteresis approximations).
- Model symmetry cue → if physics is symmetric under x→-x, v→-v, dv_dt is typically odd in x and odd in v contributions (restoring odd in x, damping odd in v).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO8)
============================================================
GT: -beta*Abs(v)**c0 - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(x,v)= -1.08868519129651\,x^3\;-\;0.600404533977091\,|v|^{1/3}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to produce **exactly** an \(x^3\) term with that coefficient, **no other \(x\)-dependence**, and a **pure** \(|v|^{1/3}\) term (not \(|v|\), not \(\log(1+k|v|)\), not \(e^{k|v|}\), not \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\), etc.), and no \(t\)-dependence.

Key obstruction used repeatedly below: with free constants you can *remove* extra terms by setting their coefficients to 0, but you **cannot** turn \(\log(1+a|v|)\), \(e^{a|v|}\), \(\sin(\log(1+a|v|)+\phi)\), \(|v|\), \(|v|\cdot e^{a|v|}\), etc. into \(|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\). Also, any appearance of \(v\) without Abs (odd in \(v\)) cannot equal an even function of \(v\) unless its coefficient is 0.

---

### Candidate-by-candidate

1. \(c0 + c1 x^3 + c2\log(c3|v|+1)+c4 e^{c5|v|}+c6 e^{c7|v|}\log(c8|v|+1)\)  
   Can set \(c0=0\), \(c1=-1.0886...\), and kill exp/log terms by setting their coefficients to 0. But then there is **no way** to get \(|v|^{1/3}\) because only log/exp structures exist. **No match**.

2. \(c0 x^3 + c1|v| + \dots + c9|v|\) plus logs/exp/constant  
   You can fit \(x^3\), and you can remove logs/exp/constant, but remaining \( |v|\) is linear in \(|v|\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

3. Like (1) plus \(c9 x^3|x|\)  
   Must set \(c9=0\) to avoid \(x^3|x|\) (not equal to \(x^3\) globally). Still only log/exp for \(v\). **No match**.

4. \(c0 x^3 + c1|v| + c3 e^{c4 x} + \dots\)  
   Must kill \(e^{c4 x}\) term (set \(c3=0\)) to avoid non-polynomial \(x\). Still only \(|v|\)/exp/log forms, not \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

5. Same issue as (1) but with an added \(c8|v|\). Linear \(|v|\) cannot become \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

6. \(c0 x^3 + c1|v| + c3 e^{c4|v|} + c5 e^{c6|v|}\log(\cdot)\)  
   Even after killing exp/log, only \(|v|\) remains. **No match**.

7. Contains \(c0 e^{c1 x}\), \(\sin(\log(1+\cdot))\), and \(x/(c9+|x|)^3\)  
   Must set coefficients of these extra \(x\)-dependent terms to 0 to keep only \(x^3\). Then no \(|v|^{1/3}\) term remains (only sine-of-log possible, which cannot equal a power globally). **No match**.

8. Like (7) plus \(c8 v e^{c9 t}\)  
   Any nonzero \(c8\) introduces odd-in-\(v\) and \(t\)-dependence; must set \(c8=0\). Then same as (7): cannot produce \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

9. Has \(c0 x\), sine-of-log, and rational \(x^{c8}/(c9+x^{c8})\)  
   GT has no \(x\) term and no rational term; must zero them out, leaving at best \(x^3\) plus sine-of-log in \(v\), which cannot equal \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

10. Adds \(v\cdot \max(0,c9+|v|)\)  
   This is odd in \(v\) when active; GT is even in \(v\). Must set \(c8=0\). Then reduces to logs/exp only for \(v\). **No match**.

11. Adds \(\max(0,c9+|v|)\)  
   Piecewise linear in \(|v|\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\). If set \(c8=0\), no \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

12. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 \sin(c3\log(1+c4|v|)+c6)\)  
   Must set \(c0=0\). Sine-of-log cannot equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) globally. **No match**.

13. Same as (12) with extra \(c7 x\)  
   Kill linear \(x\) terms; still sine-of-log issue. **No match**.

14. Polynomial in \(x\) plus \(e^{c5|v|}\) and \(e^{c7 x}\log(\cdot)\)  
   Must kill \(x^2,x\) etc. and the \(e^{c7 x}\log\) term; remaining \(e^{c5|v|}\) cannot become \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

15. \(c0 e^{c1 x} + c2 x^3 + c3 \sin(\log(1+\cdot))\)  
   Kill exp-in-\(x\). Sine-of-log cannot be \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

16. Adds \(x^5\) etc.  
   Must kill extra \(x\) powers; still only exp/log for \(v\). **No match**.

17. Same as (18) but with \(+|v|\) (fixed coefficient 1)  
   You cannot remove the \(+|v|\) term (no parameter multiplying it). GT has no \(|v|\) term. **No match**.

18. \(c0 + c1 x^3 + c2\log(1+c3|v|)+c4 e^{c5|v|}+c6\log(1+c7|v|)\)  
   Can set constant and extra terms to 0, but then no \(|v|^{1/3}\). Logs cannot equal a power globally. **No match**.

   Must kill exp-in-\(x\) and linear \(x\). Still sine-of-log. **No match**.

20. \(c0 + c1 x^3 + \log(\cdot) + e^{\cdot} + e^{\cdot}\)  
   Same: cannot produce \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

   No way to equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) globally. **No match**.

23. Two exponentials in \(x\) plus sine-of-log  
   Must kill exponentials; still sine-of-log. **No match**.

24. Adds \(\log(c9 t+1)\)  
   GT has no \(t\); must set \(c8=0\). Still sine-of-log. **No match**.

25. Has \(\sin(\log(1+c5|v|))\) and \(e^{c8 t}\)  
   Must set \(c7=0\) to remove \(t\)-dependence. Then only \(|v|\) and sine-of-log remain; cannot make \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

26. Polynomial in \(x\) plus \(e^{c8 x}\log(\cdot)\)  
   Must kill extra \(x\) terms and the \(e^{c8 x}\log\) term; remaining \(e^{c5|v|}\) cannot become \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

27. Includes \(|v|\), \(e^{\cdot}\), \(e^{\cdot}\log(\cdot)\), and \(e^{\cdot}|v|\)  
   Even if you kill exp-related terms, you’re left with \(|v|\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

28. \(c0 + c1 x^3 + c2\log(1+c3|v|) + c4 e^{c5|v|}\)  
   Same obstruction: log/exp cannot become \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

   Must kill many terms; still no \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

30. Adds \(v\cdot \max(0,c8+|v|)\) with fixed coefficient 1  
   This introduces odd-in-\(v\) behavior; cannot match even GT. No parameter to remove it. **No match**.

31. Adds \(\max(0,c8+|v|)\) with fixed coefficient 1  
   Cannot remove; GT has no such piecewise-linear term. **No match**.

32. \(c0 x^3 + (\log,\exp,\log) + c7|v|\)  
   Again only \(|v|\) and logs/exp; cannot get \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

33. \(c0 x^3 + c1|v| + c2 + c3 e^{\cdot}+c5 e^{\cdot}+ c7 \log(\cdot)\,|v|\)  
   No \(|v|^{1/3}\) possible. **No match**.

34. Has \(|v|\) and \(e^{\cdot}\sin(\cdot)\) plus high powers \(x^5,x^7\)  
   Must kill extra \(x\) powers and sinusoid term; left with \(|v|\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

   No way to reduce to \(|v|^{1/3}\) globally. **No match**.

36. \(c0 x^3 + c1|v| + c2 + c3 \sin(\log(1+c5|v|)+c6)\)  
   Cannot produce \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

37. Has \(e^{c3 x}|v|\) and \(e^{c3 x}\) etc.  
   Must kill \(x^2,x\) etc. and exp-in-\(x\) terms; still no \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

38. Includes \(\log(c8 e^{c9|v|}+1)\) etc.  
   Still log/exp compositions, not a power law. **No match**.

   Cannot get \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

   Must kill these to avoid extra \(x\)-dependence; then only \(|v|\) remains. **No match**.

   Kill extra \(x\) terms and exp-in-\(x\) term; still exp-in-\(|v|\) cannot become \(|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

   Kill \(e^{c4 x}\) and \(e^{c6|v|}\) and constant; left with \(|v|\). **No match**.

   Must kill \(x\) term and exp term and constant; left with \(|v|\). **No match**.

   (because terms with \(|x|/(|x|+1)\) plus \(1/(|x|+1)\) sum to 1). Must set \(c6=0\). Still only log/exp for \(v\). **No match**.

47. \(c0 + c1 x^3 + c2\log(\cdot) + c4 e^{c5|v|}\sin(c6 x+c7)\)  
   To avoid extra \(x\)-dependence from \(\sin(c6 x+c7)\), must set \(c4=0\). Then only log for \(v\). **No match**.

48. \( (c0+c2)x^3 + c1|v| + c3 + c4 e^{c5|v|}\sin(c6 x+c7) + c8 x\)  
   Must kill sine term and linear \(x\) and constant; left with \(|v|\). **No match**.

49. \(c0 + c1 x^3 + c2\log(\cdot)+c4 e^{c5|v|} + c6 x/(c7+|x|)^2\)  
   Must set \(c6=0\). Still log/exp for \(v\). **No match**.

50. Polynomial in \(x\) plus \(c2|v| + c3|x| + e^{c7|v|}\sin(\cdot)\)  
   Must kill \(|x|\) term (cannot equal polynomial globally) and sinusoid term; left with \(|v|\). **No match**.

No candidate contains a free-parameter term of the form \(k\,|v|^{p}\) where \(p\) can be set to \(1/3\). All \(v\)-dependence is via \(|v|\), \(\log(1+a|v|)\), \(e^{a|v|}\), products thereof, max/hinge, or sine-of-log, none of which can equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\). Therefore none can be made identical to the GT.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO8)
============================================================
GT: -beta*Abs(v)**c0 - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -1.08868519129651·x³ - 0.600404533977091·|v|^(1/3)**

The GT has exactly two terms: a cubic in x and a cube-root of |v|. No constant offset, no exponentials, no logarithms, no linear terms, no x² terms, etc.

For a candidate to match, all extra basis functions must be eliminable (by setting their coefficients to 0), and the remaining terms must be able to represent both `-c·x³` and `-c·|v|^(1/3)`.

The key challenge: **|v|^(1/3) is a specific function**. Can any combination of log, exp, |v|, sin(log(...)), etc. exactly equal |v|^(1/3) for all v? Generally no — these are linearly independent basis functions.

Let me check each candidate:

**Candidates with log/exp combinations trying to match |v|^(1/3):**
Candidates 1-6, 10-11, 17-18, 20, 27-28, 30-35, 38, 42-43, 45-46, 49: These use combinations of log(c·|v|+1), exp(c·|v|), |v|, etc. None of these basis functions can combine to exactly equal |v|^(1/3) for all v. The functions log(c·|v|+1), exp(c·|v|), and |v| are linearly independent from |v|^(1/3). **[NO MATCH]** for all of these.

**Candidates with sin(c·log(c·|v|+1)+c) terms:**
Candidates 7-9, 12-13, 15, 19, 21-25, 36, 44: These contain sin(c₃·log(c₄·|v|+1)+c₅). Note that if we set the argument's log coefficient appropriately... but sin(c·log(|v|+1)) cannot equal |v|^(1/3) for all v. Even log(|v|) composed with sin gives oscillatory behavior, not a power law. **[NO MATCH]** for all.

**Candidate 22:** Has two sin(log) terms. Still can't produce |v|^(1/3). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates with exp(c·x) terms (14, 16, 26, 29, 37, 40, 41):** Even setting exp terms to zero, the remaining terms involve log/exp/|v| in v, which can't match |v|^(1/3). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates 34, 39, 50:** Include exp·sin terms and polynomial terms in x. Can't produce |v|^(1/3). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates 47, 48:** exp·sin terms. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 46:** Simplify: each pair like `c0·|x|/(|x|+1) + c0/(|x|+1) = c0·(|x|+1)/(|x|+1) = c0`. Similarly for other terms. So it simplifies to: `c0 + c1·x³ + c2·log(c3·|v|+1) + c4·exp(c5·|v|) + c6·x/(|x|+1)`. Still can't match |v|^(1/3). **[NO MATCH]**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain |v|^(1/3) or any combination of functions that can exactly reproduce |v|^(1/3) across all values of v.
